```
<btiffin@canada.com> wrote in message 
news:43ac19f9-2442-47d4-bffb-e38d6bb0340c@e18g2000vbe.googlegroups.com...
On Feb 15, 3:28 pm, JC <c.joyd...@gmail.com> wrote:
> William M. Klein wrote on 14-02-2009 :
>
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> and Firefox 3....

FWIW...

Much of the Microsoft documentation which specifies a minimum level of IE is 
actually a requirement for "The version of Microsoft Common Controls and/or 
Shell32 which shipped with IE<version>."

Of course it actually DOES mean "Internet Explorer"  for a few functions, 
but if the function has nothing to do with opening a URL it's likely it 
really means Common Controls and/or Shell32, both of which are routinely 
updated when new releases of IE are made available.
```

#### ↳ Re: Cobol MS-Access

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-02-15T15:45:51+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6vpduvFle0v8U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<gn7htj$1at$1@news.albasani.net>`

```
JC wrote:
> Hi,
>
> Is there any tutorial/guide available for accessing MS-Access from
> Cobol? Everything is on Windows Vista.
> Thanks for your help.

As Bill mentioned, most vendors provide sample programs in their 
documentation.

However, these are often not that good and some environments use different 
access methodologies.

For example, by default, Fujitsu COBOL will use an ODBC driver, configured 
from an external file. You CAN access using ADO or DAO (DAO is especially 
good for MS Access DBs) but there is nothing in their documentation to show 
you how. PowerCOBOL provides an ADO control, but again, explanation and 
samples are sparse.

What we need is a shared resource where the community can publish samples 
using whatever flavour of COBOL they have.

I am currently revamping the cobdata website with a view to encouraging 
this, and I'm reviewing and modernising a lot of documents I have lying 
about, some of which deal with accessing RDBs in COBOL, specifically, MS 
ACCESS from Fujitsu.

If you understand OOP, then it is very simple to just use an Automation 
(COM) server to connect to whatever you want in MS Office: ACCESS, Excel, 
Word, PowerPoint, and so on. Without this knowledge it is a more difficult 
road, although it is quite passable.  We saw hundreds of lines of COBOL code 
here recently to enable production of  a .PDF from a web page; in .NET, 
using Automation, it is 3 lines in C# and about 10 in COBOL...(both running 
server side). It baffles me why people seem to prefer complex solutions.

In the meantime, have a look at the thread: "Fujitsu NetCOBOL 8" in this 
forum.

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: Cobol MS-Access

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <mmattias@talsystems.com>
- **Date:** 2009-02-15T07:57:52-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8cVll.17826$c45.3913@nlpi065.nbdc.sbc.com>`
- **References:** `<gn7htj$1at$1@news.albasani.net>`

```
> Is there any tutorial/guide available for accessing MS-Access from Cobol? 
> Everything is on Windows Vista.
> Thanks for your help.

If you can find any documentation on using the OLE provider via ADO, that 
will work. If you can find any documentation on using ODBC, that will work, 
too.

Both OLE via ADO and ODBC are "specific-DBMS-product agnostic". (well I 
"suppose" you could try the direct OLE interface, but that is really hairy, 
and with ADO available it would be IMO silly to not use it).

FWIW, with both OLE and ODBC interfaces, if you can find something which 
manipulates MS-Excel spreadsheets, other than the connection string the code 
will be the same,although the way tables are named in SQL statements is 
kinda funny with excel (using Jet/Access, you refer to table names as, well, 
the name of the table; for Excel spreadsheets the "table" name is expressed 
as "[worksheet_name]"

I do not believe there is an ESQL compiler  ( "EXEC SQL ... END-EXEC ") 
specifically for the Jet/Access DBMS, although there may well be one for 
OLE/ADO; and I am positive there is no direct "client interface API" you can 
call.
```

#### ↳ Re: Cobol MS-Access

- **From:** foxgrove@shaw.ca
- **Date:** 2009-02-17T08:43:45-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<feb8e1bb-edaf-448e-8d25-706dbe7cf282@w24g2000prd.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<gn7htj$1at$1@news.albasani.net>`

```
On Feb 14, 4:51 pm, JC <c.joyd...@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hi,
>
> Is there any tutorial/guide available for accessing MS-Access from
> Cobol? Everything is on Windows Vista.
> Thanks for your help.

here is an extract of a program I wrote for MicroFocus to create and
load a spreadsheet
and, yes it is ugly
but, yes it works

      $set ooctrl(+P)
       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
       PROGRAM-ID.      EXCEL01.
       AUTHOR.          CG.
       DATE-WRITTEN.    March 2005.

       ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
       CONFIGURATION SECTION.
       SPECIAL-NAMES.
           call-convention 66 is WIN32APIDYN.
       INPUT-OUTPUT SECTION.
       FILE-CONTROL.

       CLASS-CONTROL.
           MicrosoftExcel is class "$OLE$Excel.Application"
           EntryPointCallback is class "entrycll"
           ExceptionManager is class "exptnmgr"
           AutomationExceptionManager is class "oleexpt"
           AutomationSupport is class "olesup".

 
*****************************************************************
       DATA DIVISION.
       FILE SECTION.

 
*****************************************************************
       WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
 
*****************************************************************
       copy "TypeLib.cpy".

       01  Excel                           OBJECT REFERENCE.
       01  NullReference                   OBJECT REFERENCE VALUE
NULL.
       01  HandlerObject                   OBJECT REFERENCE.
       01  Workbooks                       OBJECT REFERENCE.
       01  Workbook                        OBJECT REFERENCE.
       01  WorkSheets                      OBJECT REFERENCE.
       01  WorkSheet                       OBJECT REFERENCE.
       01  Cell                            OBJECT REFERENCE.
       01  CellRange                       OBJECT REFERENCE.
       01  FloatValue                      COMP-1.
       01  ErrorOccurred                   PIC 9       VALUE 0.
       01  FileFilter                      PIC X(46) VALUE
           z"Excel Files (*.xls),*.xls,All Files (*.*),*.*".

       01  FileName.
           05         PIC X(29) VALUE "M:\OE-XLS\TIME_SHEET_SUMMARY_".
           05              PIC X(4)    VALUE ".xls".

       01  Indexes.
           05  RowIndex                    PIC XX COMP-5.
           05  ColumnIndex                 PIC XX COMP-5.

       01  STORAGE.
           05  WS-CELL-VALUE               PIC X(120).
           05  WS-CELL-VALUE-LEN           PIC 9999.
           05  WS-TOTAL-ROW                PIC X(4).

       01  shrink-in.
           05  sin  pic x occurs 120.
       01  shrink-out.
           05  sot pic x occurs 120.
       01  shrink-a pic 999.
       01  shrink-b pic 999.
       01  shrink-LINE-LEN                 PIC X(4) COMP-5.

       LOCAL-STORAGE SECTION.

       LINKAGE SECTION.
       01  ErrorNumber                     PIC X(4) COMP-5.
       01  ErrorObject                     OBJECT REFERENCE.
       01  ErrorText                       OBJECT REFERENCE.

 
******************************************************************
       PROCEDURE DIVISION.
 
******************************************************************
       100-START-SECTION             SECTION.
       100-START-PROGRAM.

           PERFORM 8000-CREATE-EXCEL.
           PERFORM 8100-LOAD-EXCEL-HEADERS.
           PERFORM 8200-LOAD-EXCEL-DETAIL.
           PERFORM 8300-LOAD-EXCEL-TOTALS.
           PERFORM 8500-LOAD-EXCEL-FOOTERS.
           PERFORM 8600-SAVE-EXCEL.
           PERFORM 8700-CLOSE-EXCEL.

       990-EXIT.
           EXIT PROGRAM.
       999-EOJ.
           STOP RUN.

 
******************************************************************
       8000-Create-Excel.
 
******************************************************************
      *    create a new instance of Excel and make visible
           INVOKE EntryPointCallback "new" USING
z"AutomationException"
                                           RETURNING HandlerObject

           INVOKE ExceptionManager "register"
                                   USING AutomationExceptionManager
                                         HandlerObject

           INVOKE MicrosoftExcel "new" RETURNING Excel
      *    error handling
           IF ErrorOccurred = 1
               display "Unable to load the Automation Server"
               STOP RUN
           END-IF

           INVOKE Excel "setVisible" USING BY VALUE Automation-True

           INVOKE Excel "getWorkBooks" RETURNING WorkBooks

           INVOKE Workbooks "Add" RETURNING Workbook

           INVOKE Workbook "getWorkSheets" RETURNING WorkSheets

           INVOKE WorkSheets "getItem" USING BY VALUE 1
                                           RETURNING WorkSheet.

 
******************************************************************
       8100-Load-Excel-Headers.
 
******************************************************************
           MOVE 1 TO RowIndex
           MOVE 1 TO ColumnIndex
           MOVE SS-HEAD-2 TO WS-CELL-VALUE
           PERFORM 8800-LOAD-CELL

      * WEEK 1
           ADD 1 TO RowIndex
           MOVE 1 TO ColumnIndex
      *    Regular Hours
           MOVE "Regular Hours" TO WS-CELL-VALUE
           PERFORM 8800-LOAD-CELL
      *    Overtime
           ADD 1 to ColumnIndex
           MOVE "Overtime" TO WS-CELL-VALUE
           PERFORM 8800-LOAD-CELL
           .

 
******************************************************************
       8200-Load-Excel-Detail.
 
******************************************************************
           ADD 1 TO RowIndex
           MOVE 1 TO ColumnIndex
           MOVE SS-TOTREG1 TO WS-CELL-VALUE      *> week 1 reg hours
           PERFORM 8800-LOAD-CELL
           ADD 1 TO ColumnIndex
           MOVE SS-TOTOVR1 TO WS-CELL-VALUE      *> week 1 overtime
           PERFORM 8800-LOAD-CELL
           .

 
******************************************************************
       8300-Load-Excel-Totals.
 
******************************************************************
           MOVE RowIndex to WS-TOTAL-ROW
           ADD 2 TO RowIndex

           MOVE 1 TO ColumnIndex
           STRING "=SUM(A3:A" WS-TOTAL-ROW ")" INTO WS-CELL-VALUE
           PERFORM 8800-LOAD-CELL
           ADD 1 TO ColumnIndex
           STRING "=SUM(B3:B" WS-TOTAL-ROW ")" INTO WS-CELL-VALUE
           PERFORM 8800-LOAD-CELL
           .

 
******************************************************************
       8500-Load-Excel-Footers.
 
******************************************************************
           ADD 3 TO RowIndex
           MOVE 1 TO ColumnIndex
           MOVE SS-BOTT-1 TO WS-CELL-VALUE
           PERFORM 8800-LOAD-CELL
           ADD 1 TO RowIndex
           MOVE SS-BOTT-2 TO WS-CELL-VALU
           .

 
******************************************************************
       8600-Save-Excel.
 
******************************************************************
           INVOKE WorkSheet "SaveAs" USING FILENAME
           .

 
******************************************************************
       8700-Close-Excel.
 
******************************************************************
           INVOKE Workbook "Close" USING BY VALUE 0
           INVOKE WorkSheet "Finalize" RETURNING WorkSheet
           INVOKE WorkSheets "Finalize" RETURNING WorkSheets
           INVOKE WorkBook "Finalize" RETURNING WorkBook
           INVOKE WorkBooks "Finalize" RETURNING WorkBooks
           INVOKE Excel "Quit"
           INVOKE Excel "Finalize" RETURNING Excel
           .

 
******************************************************************
       8800-LOAD-CELL.
 
******************************************************************
           INVOKE Excel "getCells" USING BY VALUE RowIndex
                                         BY VALUE ColumnIndex
                                         RETURNING Cell
           MOVE WS-CELL-VALUE TO SHRINK-IN
           PERFORM SHRINK-COMMAND THRU SHRINK-COMMAND-EXIT
           INVOKE Cell "setValue" USING SHRINK-OUT(1:SHRINK-LINE-LEN)
           INVOKE Cell "Finalize" RETURNING Cell
           MOVE SPACES TO WS-CELL-VALUE
           .

 
******************************************************************
       shrink-command.
      * change all multiple spaces to single spaces
      * input is shrink-in, output is shrink-out
           move space to shrink-out.
           move 1 to shrink-a.
           move 1 to shrink-b.
       shrink-loop1.
           move sin (shrink-a) to sot (shrink-b).
           add 1 to shrink-a.
           add 1 to shrink-b.
           if shrink-a > 120 go to shrink-done.
           if sin (shrink-a) not = " "
               go to shrink-loop1.
           add 1 to shrink-b.
       shrink-loop2.
           add 1 to shrink-a.
           if shrink-a > 120 go to shrink-done.
           if sin (shrink-a) = " "
               go to shrink-loop2.
           go to shrink-loop1.
       shrink-done.
           move shrink-b to  shrink-line-len.
       shrink-command-exit.
           exit.

 
******************************************************************
       CALLBACK SECTION.
 
******************************************************************
       ENTRY "AutomationException"
           USING BY REFERENCE ErrorObject
                 BY REFERENCE ErrorNumber
                 BY REFERENCE ErrorText.
           MOVE 1 TO ErrorOccurred
           DISPLAY "ErrorNumber:" ErrorNumber
           INVOKE ErrorText "DISPLAY"
           EXIT PROGRAM RETURNING NullReference.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Cobol MS-Access

- **From:** "James J. Gavan" <jgavandeletethis@shaw.ca>
- **Date:** 2009-02-18T16:50:25-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<691nl.22173$uG1.15255@newsfe16.iad>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<feb8e1bb-edaf-448e-8d25-706dbe7cf282@w24g2000prd.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<gn7htj$1at$1@news.albasani.net> <feb8e1bb-edaf-448e-8d25-706dbe7cf282@w24g2000prd.googlegroups.com>`

```
foxgrove@shaw.ca wrote:
> On Feb 14, 4:51 pm, JC <c.joyd...@gmail.com> wrote:
> 
…[32 more quoted lines elided]…
>  
etc....

Agree, it is ugly :-). Not that you've got much choice with OLE and the
concept works fine with MS Excel and Word - but it's not the route I'd
choose to go with MS Access. That's a DB like any other, and you can
work without worrying about OLE.

If you don't like the OO approach in the following, just convert to a
Procedural Program turning the method-starts into 'Entry Points'.

1. File generated from OpenESQL Assistant using the MS Access DB :-

*>----------------------------------------------------------------
    EXEC SQL DECLARE
      `Descriptions` TABLE
      ( "DesID"             VARCHAR(2)
       ,"DesCode"           VARCHAR(4)
       ,"DesName"           VARCHAR(40)
       ,"DesOther1"         VARCHAR(10)
       ,"DesOther2"         VARCHAR(10)
       ,"DesUpdated"        VARCHAR(16)
    ) END-EXEC
******************************************************************
* COBOL DECLARATION FOR TABLE Descriptions                       *
******************************************************************
  01  DCLTable.
      03 A-DesPrimeKey.
         05 A-DesID         PIC X(2).
         05 A-DesCode       PIC X(4).
      03 A-DesName          PIC X(40).
      03 A-DesOther1        PIC X(10).
      03 A-DesOther2        PIC X(10).
      03 A-DesUpdated       PIC X(16).
******************************************************************
* COBOL INDICATOR VARIABLES FOR TABLE                            *
******************************************************************
  01  DCLTable-NULL.
      03 A-DesID-NULL       PIC S9(04)  COMP-5.
      03 A-DesCode-NULL     PIC S9(04)  COMP-5.
      03 A-DesName-NULL     PIC S9(04)  COMP-5.
      03 A-DesOther1-NULL   PIC S9(04)  COMP-5.
      03 A-DesOther2-NULL   PIC S9(04)  COMP-5.
      03 A-DesUpdated-NULL  PIC S9(04)  COMP-5.

*****************************************************************

2. A Class used for accessing the above. Note TableDescrips inherits
from SQlConnect, which in turn inherits from SQLErrors.

$set sql (dbman=ODBC)
$set ooctrl (+W)
  *>-----------------tabledescrips.cbl----------------------------

  Class-id.          DescriptionsTable
                     data is protected
                     inherits from SqlConnection.

  Class-control.     CharacterArray       is class "chararry"
                     DateAndTime          is class "datetime"
                     DescriptionsTable    is class "tabledescrips"
                     SqlConnection        is class "sqlconnect"
                     .
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  *>FACTORY.
  *>END FACTORY.
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  OBJECT.
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------

  *> Using the appropriate table in MS Access, the SQL Statements
  *> are generated in the N/E IDE - OpenESQL Assistant module - and
  *> are then copy/pasted into the source below

  WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
  EXEC SQL INCLUDE SQLCA END-EXEC

  copy "Descriptions.cpy".
  copy "\copylib\sqlerror.cpy" replacing ==(tag)== by ==ws==.

  01 ws-dbID               pic 9 value 1. *> General
  78 RecordLength          value 82.
  01 ws-RecordLength       pic x(4) comp-5 value 82.
  01 DBFlag                pic 9 value 2.
     88 SingleDB           value 1.
     88 MultiDB            value 2.

  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "begin".
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Linkage section.
  01 lnk-Parent                      object reference.

  Procedure Division using lnk-Parent.
     invoke super "setParent" using lnk-Parent
  *> compute ws-RecordLength = function length (DCLTable)

  End Method "begin".
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "checkForRectype".    *> SELECT DISTINCT
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Linkage section.
  01 lnk-rectype                      pic x(02).
  copy "\copylib\sqlResult.cpy" replacing ==(tag)== by ==01 lnk==.

  Procedure Division using lnk-rectype
                    returning lnk-SqlResult.

   set ResultOK to true

   if   MultiDB
        invoke super "setCurrentConnection"
        using ws-dbID returning lnk-SqlResult

        if TableError
           EXIT METHOD
        end-if
   end-if

   move lnk-Rectype to A-DesID

       EXEC SQL
        SELECT DISTINCT
               `A`.`DesID`
        INTO
             :A-DesID:A-DesID-NULL
          FROM `Descriptions` A
         WHERE ( `A`.`DesID` = A-DesID )
       END-EXEC

   Evaluate true
       when SQLSTATE = "00000"
            continue
       when SQLSTATE = "02000"              *> No more rows
            set RecNotFound to true
       when other
            invoke self "PrepareErrorMessage"
            set TableError to true
   End-Evaluate

  End Method "checkForRectype".
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "deleteRow".     *> DELETE
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Linkage section.
  01 lnk-Key.
     05 lnk-DesID                pic x(02).      *> = Record Type
     05 lnk-DesCode              pic x(04).
  copy "\copylib\sqlResult.cpy" replacing ==(tag)== by ==01 lnk==.

  Procedure Division using     lnk-Key
                     returning lnk-SqlResult.

   set ResultOK to true

   if   MultiDB
        invoke super "setCurrentConnection"
        using ws-dbID returning lnk-SqlResult

        if TableError
           EXIT METHOD
        end-if
   end-if

     move lnk-DesId   to A-DesID
     move lnk-DesCode to A-DesCode

       EXEC SQL
        DELETE FROM `Descriptions`
         WHERE ( `DesID` = :A-DesID )
          AND  ( `DesCode` = :A-DesCode )
       END-EXEC

     Evaluate true
        when SQLSTATE = "00000"
             EXEC SQL COMMIT END-EXEC
             set ResultOK to true
        when SQLSTATE = "02000"           *> No more rows
             set RecNotFound to true
        when other
             invoke self "PrepareErrorMessage"
             set TableError to true
    End-evaluate

  End Method "deleteRow".
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "FinalizeObjects".
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  *> Nothing to do - this class doesn't create any objects

  End Method "FinalizeObjects".
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "InsertRow".        *> "WRITE"
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Linkage section.
  01 lnk-record           pic x(RecordLength).
  copy "\copylib\sqlResult.cpy" replacing ==(tag)== by ==01 lnk==.

  Procedure Division  using     lnk-Record
                      returning lnk-SqlResult.

   move lnk-record to DCLTable
   set ResultOK    to true

   if   MultiDB
        invoke super "setCurrentConnection"
        using ws-dbID returning lnk-SqlResult

        if TableError
           EXIT METHOD
        end-if
   end-if

  invoke DateAndTime "getDateModified" returning A-DesUpdated

       EXEC SQL
        INSERT INTO `Descriptions`
        (`DesID`
        ,`DesCode`
        ,`DesName`
        ,`DesOther1`
        ,`DesOther2`
        ,`DesUpdated`
        ) VALUES
        (:A-DesID:A-DesID-NULL
        ,:A-DesCode:A-DesCode-NULL
        ,:A-DesName:A-DesName-NULL
        ,:A-DesOther1:A-DesOther1-NULL
        ,:A-DesOther2:A-DesOther2-NULL
        ,:A-DesUpdated:A-DesUpdated-NULL
        )
       END-EXEC

     Evaluate true
       when SQLSTATE = "00000"
            EXEC SQL COMMIT END-EXEC
       when other
            invoke self "PrepareErrorMessage"
            set TableError to true
     End-evaluate

  End Method "InsertRow".
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "makeCollection".   *> CURSOR SELECT DISTINCT
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  *> This is my 'normal' "MakeCollection" - primarily used to
  *> build a Collection 'ofReferences' to display in GUI
  *> dialogs - BUT - always possibility of 'ofValues', i.e.
  *> 'text strings'

  *> Note that the empty Collection is passed to this Class through
  *> Linkage - but is NOT returned to the invoker when elements
  *> have been used to populate the Collection - The Invoker
  *> object reference to this Collection "knows" what has been added

  *> For this particular Table, rows are extracted based on a two-
  *> character record-type.

  WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
  01 ls-TempObject                object reference.
  Linkage section.
  01 lnk-DesKey                   pic x(02).
  01 lnk-Flag                     pic 9.
     88 ofValues                  value 1.
     88 ofReferences              value 2.
  01 lnk-Collection               object reference.

  copy "\copylib\sqlResult.cpy" replacing ==(tag)== by ==01 lnk==.

  Procedure Division using     lnk-DesKey
                               lnk-Flag
                               lnk-Collection
                     returning lnk-SqlResult.

   set ResultOK to true

   if   MultiDB
        invoke super "setCurrentConnection"
        using ws-dbID returning lnk-SqlResult

        if TableError
           EXIT METHOD
        end-if
   end-if

  move lnk-DesKey to DCLTABLE (1:2)

       EXEC SQL
        DECLARE CSR25 CURSOR FOR SELECT DISTINCT
               `A`.`DesID`
              ,`A`.`DesCode`
              ,`A`.`DesName`
              ,`A`.`DesOther1`
              ,`A`.`DesOther2`
              ,`A`.`DesUpdated`
          FROM `Descriptions` A
         WHERE ( `A`.`DesID` = `A`.`DesID` )
       END-EXEC
       EXEC SQL OPEN CSR25 END-EXEC
       PERFORM UNTIL SQLSTATE <> "00000"
         EXEC SQL
         FETCH CSR25 INTO
             :A-DesID:A-DesID-NULL
            ,:A-DesCode:A-DesCode-NULL
            ,:A-DesName:A-DesName-NULL
            ,:A-DesOther1:A-DesOther1-NULL
            ,:A-DesOther2:A-DesOther2-NULL
            ,:A-DesUpdated:A-DesUpdated-NULL
         END-EXEC

          Evaluate true

             when SQLSTATE = "00000"

               Evaluate true
                 when ofReferences
                    invoke CharacterArray "withLengthValue"
                        using     ws-RecordLength DCLTable
                        returning ls-TempObject
                    invoke lnk-Collection "add" using ls-TempObject

                 when other
                     invoke lnk-Collection "add" using DCLTable
               End-evaluate

             when SQLSTATE = "02000"
                  set NoMoreRows to true
                  EXIT PERFORM
             when other
                  invoke self "PrepareErrorMessage"
                  set TableError to true
                  EXIT PERFORM
           End-evaluate

       END-PERFORM

       EXEC SQL CLOSE CSR25 END-EXEC

  End Method "makeCollection".
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "PrepareErrorMessage".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------

       move "Key : "             to ws-ErrorID
       move A-DesPrimeKey        to ws-ErrorID (7:6)
       move SQLSTATE             to ws-SqlState
       move "Descriptions Table" to ws-TableName
       invoke super "sqlStateMessage" using ws-ErrorParams

  End Method "PrepareErrorMessage".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "readRow".        *> SELECT DISTINCT
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Linkage section.
  01 lnk-key.
     05 IN-DesID                    pic 9(02).
     05 IN-DesCode                  pic x(04).

  01 lnk-reKord.
   copy "\copylib\sqlResult.cpy" replacing ==(tag)== by ==05 lnk==.
   05 lnk-record           pic x(RecordLength).

  Procedure Division using     lnk-key
                     returning lnk-reKord.

   set ResultOK to true

   if   MultiDB
        invoke super "setCurrentConnection"
        using ws-dbID returning lnk-SqlResult

        if TableError
           EXIT METHOD
        end-if
   end-if

   move IN-DesID    to A-DesID
   move IN-DesCode  to A-DesCode

       EXEC SQL
        SELECT DISTINCT
               `A`.`DesID`
              ,`A`.`DesCode`
              ,`A`.`DesName`
              ,`A`.`DesOther1`
              ,`A`.`DesOther2`
              ,`A`.`DesUpdated`
        INTO
             :A-DesID:A-DesID-NULL
            ,:A-DesCode:A-DesCode-NULL
            ,:A-DesName:A-DesName-NULL
            ,:A-DesOther1:A-DesOther1-NULL
            ,:A-DesOther2:A-DesOther2-NULL
            ,:A-DesUpdated:A-DesUpdated-NULL
          FROM `Descriptions` A
         WHERE ( `A`.`DesID` = :A-DesID )
          AND  ( `A`.`DesCode` = :A-DesCode )
       END-EXEC

   Evaluate true
       when SQLSTATE = "00000"
            move DCLTable to lnk-record
       when SQLSTATE = "02000"              *> No more rows
            set RecNotFound to true
       when other
            invoke self "PrepareErrorMessage"
             set TableError to true
   End-Evaluate

  End Method "readRow".
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "setDBflag".
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
  Linkage section.
  01 lnk-DBflag            pic 9.

  Procedure Division using lnk-DBflag.
  move lnk-DBflag to DBFlag
  End Method "setDBflag".
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Method-id. "UpdateRow".          *> REWRITE
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------
  Linkage section.
  01 lnk-record               pic x(RecordLength).
  copy "\copylib\sqlResult.cpy" replacing ==(tag)== by ==01 lnk==.

  Procedure Division using lnk-record
                     returning lnk-SqlResult.

   set ResultOK to true

   if   MultiDB
        invoke super "setCurrentConnection"
        using ws-dbID returning lnk-SqlResult

        if TableError
           EXIT METHOD
        end-if
   end-if

   move lnk-record to DCLTable
   invoke DateAndTime "getDateModified" returning A-DesUpdated

  EXEC SQL
   UPDATE `Descriptions`
    SET `DesID` = :A-DesID:A-DesID-NULL
       ,`DesCode` = :A-DesCode:A-DesCode-NULL
       ,`DesName` = :A-DesName:A-DesName-NULL
       ,`DesOther1` = :A-DesOther1:A-DesOther1-NULL
       ,`DesOther2` = :A-DesOther2:A-DesOther2-NULL
       ,`DesUpdated` = :A-DesUpdated:A-DesUpdated-NULL
     WHERE ( `DesID` = :A-DesID )
      AND  ( `DesCode` = :A-DesCode )
  END-EXEC

   Evaluate true
      when SQLSTATE = "00000"
        EXEC SQL COMMIT END-EXEC
      when other
        invoke self "PrepareErrorMessage"
        set TableError to true
   End-evaluate

  End Method "UpdateRow".
  *>--------------------------------------------------------------

  END OBJECT.
  End CLASS DescriptionsTable.
  *>---------------------------------------------------------------
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Cobol MS-Access

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-02-19T16:05:09+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7040j6Fmql6jU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<gn7htj$1at$1@news.albasani.net> <feb8e1bb-edaf-448e-8d25-706dbe7cf282@w24g2000prd.googlegroups.com> <691nl.22173$uG1.15255@newsfe16.iad>`

```
James J. Gavan wrote:
> foxgrove@shaw.ca wrote:
<snipped examples of accessing MS Excel via OLE and MS ACCESS via ODBC using 
Micro Focus COBOL.>

The consideration that needs to be examined here is how important efficiency 
is to the end result.

While I wouldn't agree that either of the solutions offered is "ugly", 
neither of them is particularly "elegant" either.

ODBC is flexisble and allows connection to any database that provides an 
ODBC driver, sometimes without requiring any change to the COBOL code, BUT 
it is NOT efficient (compared to other options).

Cursors in ODBC hold the DB connection for as long as the cursor is open. 
This can have a very serious effect on throughput where multiple databases 
are being accessed from multiple terminals. New connections may have to wait 
to obtain a connection and this can be a "bottleneck"  which degrades 
overall system throughput. This factor alone is a major one in the 
deprecation of Embedded SQL (ESQL). (Many programmers see ESQL as being 
obsolete, replacing it with multiset constructs and triggered stored 
procedures...There are some very compelling arguments for doing this 
anyway...)

Automation (OLE originally, now COM) provides platform independent access 
and (for MS ACCESS in particular, but not exclusively) enables the use of 
DAO or ADO, both of which are many times more efficient than ODBC. ADO can 
be used with a number of databases besides MS-ACCESS and it runs a single 
query which returns a resultset, then disconnects. Connections are held for 
milliseconds rather than minutes and the resultset is processed in memory. 
DAO, although deprecated by Microsoft in favour of ADO, is a "no frills" 
package which runs very efficiently with ACCESS. You can run ADO and DAO 
from COBOL but you will need to use COM/OLE to establish easy communication 
with these subsystems. (COM is not the ONLY way but it is probably the best 
way for COBOL...)

I tried using ADO with dynamic SQL from COBOL and found that even with the 
dynamic PREPAREs it was STILL considerably faster than ESQL across ODBC.

These days I use LINQ with C# to access databases and I have no intention of 
going back to ESQL and ODBC; it is simply a different world.

The point of my post is that before we label anything as "ugly" we should 
look at the context it is intended for. Many things that we think are 
"cool", in a broader context can be seen to be not so...

Pete.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Cobol MS-Access

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2009-02-19T13:07:50+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<gnjlj6$nvh$1@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<gn7htj$1at$1@news.albasani.net> <feb8e1bb-edaf-448e-8d25-706dbe7cf282@w24g2000prd.googlegroups.com> <691nl.22173$uG1.15255@newsfe16.iad> <7040j6Fmql6jU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
In article <7040j6Fmql6jU1@mid.individual.net>,
Pete Dashwood <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:

[snip]

>Cursors in ODBC hold the DB connection for as long as the cursor is open. 
>This can have a very serious effect on throughput where multiple databases 
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>deprecation of Embedded SQL (ESQL).

I recall being taught - back in the Oldene Dayse, when DB2 releases still 
had a '1' to the left of the decimal point/period/full stop - that cursors 
had one major advantage and one major disadvatage.

The advantage was that they could be used to individually address rows 
which, due to database design (or lack thereof), would be multiply 
returned by a SELECT; this was a Good Thing because it allowed companies 
to skimp on training and design by telling their programmers 'It is just 
like accessing a VSAM file by a START KEY NOT < and then a READ NEXT'.

(Never mind that this attitude discouraged folks from using a database as 
a database... it Saved Money and Kept Things As 'We' Knew them, things 
that are *very* important in some organisations)

The disadvantage was called 'cursor drag'... that the opening of the 
cursor created, in effect, a snapshot of the subset of the rows which 
reflected the cursor's definition... and it takes DASD and CPU to first 
create these, then address them by FETCHes and UPDATEs and the like, 
create the transaction rollback entries in case something crashes and 
then, finally, CLOSE the cursor, apply the changes (if any), empty the 
rollback logs and COMMIT the whole mess.

In short... when in doubt, blame it on 'cursor drag'; when enough of that 
happens a committee/task group will be formed to look into the matter and 
maybe even make a few recommendations about redesign... which, of course, 
will be accepted with their usual delight.

DD
```

```
Very interesting to me. I am in the process of migrating a couple of my 
applications from ODBC to OLE via ADO.  Being new to ADO,  I started with an 
application which does not need to do prepares/binding etc because if  has 
twenty rows to insert or update at one time, that's a LOT.

or tens of thousands of inserts per run), and I was worried about 
performance.

creating an ODBC datasource on customer systems (even though I create the 
original one for them during the install); plus the requirement to find and 
install an ODBC 3.x  driver  for Oracle (I need the transaction management 
so the 2x driver which comes with Windows is just not good enough) for my 
customers who want to use PPPS on an Oracle system has just proven to be 
'too much' for many of my smaller customers.
```

```
> James J. Gavan wrote:
> > foxgr...@shaw.ca wrote:
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> is to the end result.

That is not just whether it is ODBC or ADO or ESQL or ...

The database system used has a major effect on performance and this
also depends on how the db is used.

I am having to do some extracts from a system to send to a MSSQL
server. I did some Python that extracted data from a Cobol system and
formatted it up as SQL CREATEs and INSERTs. The text file ran to about
100 Mbyte and then I pushed this into PostgreSQL using psql (batch
command line). The whole thing (extract and load) ran in about 20
minutes on a Linux box - single CPU around 2GHz.

There was only a slow link to the MSSQL server so I extracted a sample
from the test files and this was less than 2Mbytes so I could email
it. It was reported that this sample took 20 minutes to load into
MSSQL on a dual core 3MHz Windows machine.
```

```
Not replying for Bill.  But I've done a little bit with GTK+ for
OpenCOBOL.  The plan is a near full on binding to the GnomeToolKit,
but for now.  Buttons, Labels, Menus, File Dialog, a Calendar widget
(and a few odds and sods), enough for simple but fully functional
GUIs.

A sample screenshot and some source code can be seen at
http://add1tocobol.com/tiki-index.php?page=GTK+Sample

We've also taken Rildo's Tcl/Tk engine from TinyCOBOL and interfaced
that into OpenCOBOL as well.  For that layer most of the GUI work is
squarely on the Tk side.

Brian
```

```
On Feb 19, 11:31 am, PR <paul.rauler...@gmail.com> wrote:
> On Feb 18, 9:45 pm, btif...@canada.com wrote:
>
…[117 more quoted lines elided]…
> -Paul

New news!  New discovery (for me, perhaps old hat for others).  Vala,
http://live.gnome.org/Vala  A programming language designed for
writing code to interface with the Gnome libraries at a high level but
keeping to a C binary interface.  Vala, like OpenCOBOL, does
intermediate C so the object files are directly callable with no
linker name mangling inherent with C++ and many other higher
conceptual programming systems.

I had the valac compiler built from sources, and a GtkTreeView wrapped
in a GtkBuilder (Glade and XML ui files) called from OpenCOBOL all
within an hour.  The OpenCOBOL gui binding layer will now be orders of
magnitude easier to write and manage.  GtkBuilder was already slated
to be one of the nexts piece added to the CBL_OC_GTK_ callables, but
moving from a C based layer to the much higher conceptual Vala level
there will be a lot less glue code required.

While the posted sample doesn't really do much data passing, as I was
in a giddy rush to get the news to the OpenCOBOL folk, I've started a
thread on opencobol.org. More soon;
http://www.opencobol.org/modules/newbb/viewtopic.php?topic_id=526&forum=1&post_id=2700#forumpost2700

OpenCOBOL programmers won't really need to have a Vala compiler when
the binding layer is complete, as it can and will still be published
in object form, but as with all open things, source code will be
available and the compiler is freedom free and zero-cost free.

Very exciting.

Cheers,
Brian
```

```
Paul wrote:

> Besides, I am not at all
> sure Microfocus is even supporting GUI under LInux- they seem to be pretty
> Windows Centric lately- with .NET being their primary target.

This isn't particularly relevant to your problem - since, as you've
explained, your friend isn't in a position to use MF COBOL anyway -
but we're just as committed to our Unix / Linux product line as ever.
The MS stuff has been getting most of the press lately, and it's
certainly an area where we're doing a lot of new stuff; but new
versions of the Unix line (Server Express) are coming out on schedule,
largely from the same code base as the Windows line.

But *that* said, I don't think we actually offer a GUI facility as
such for COBOL on Unix / Linux these days. Dialog System on Unix is
character-only.

For our customers who want Unix / Linux GUIs for MF COBOL programs, we
might recommend HTML (using accept/display HTML, or AJAX plus Web
Services, or various other options), or creating a front end in Java
and using our Java interop technology.
```

#### ↳ Re: Cobol / Linux / X-Windows

- **References:** `<49979fb9$0$5472$bbae4d71@news.suddenlink.net>`

```
On Feb 15, 5:53 pm, Paul <paul-nospamatall.rauler...@mac.com> wrote:
> Oh how do I get myself into nasty little messes like this?
> A friend of mine was laid off from his job (damn bank!)
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> (damn bank! damn bank#2!)

As long as he is paid by the hour and can push the 'go live' date out
appropriately as the changes to the spec arrive then he probably can
spin this out until retirement (or even after).


> Does anyone have any experience with hooking OpenCOBOL into
> XWindows? And if so, would you be willing to share a few tips
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> now... :(

Generally text mode screens are 'program driven', that is the program
determines the sequence of interactions with the user. GUIs are
usually event driven, the user indicates what should happen.

This is not just changing the face of the application, it is changing
the way the program works, and often means a rewrite unless the
program was written originally to cope with such a change.

For GUIs on Linux I use Glade, but I haven't done this with Cobol yet,
I do it with Python. Glade has a designer which draws the screens and
generates an XML file of these. The program then 'just' has to call
glade to draw the screens and link the events to code. With Python/
Glade it just works on Linux, Windows, and my pocket computer.

I would be more inclined with Cobol to make the system run as web-
based 'in the cloud', The GUI will be frames and forms in tables with
Ajax validating the fields and lookups back to the OpenCobol code
running under Apache.

Of course this is also a complete rewrite and uses several languages
(HTML, JavaScript, Cobol).
```

```
he could spin it into a client/server on Windows or MacOS or something
he can charge a lot more money for.

Thanks -

-Paul
```

#### ↳ Re: Cobol / Linux / X-Windows

- **From:** Rene_Surop <infodynamics_ph@yahoo.com>
- **Date:** 2009-02-15T22:01:45-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7cb017d1-e616-41b9-a94e-9f3bed59159c@g39g2000pri.googlegroups.com>`

```
>
> Does anyone have any experience with hooking OpenCOBOL into
> XWindows? And if so, would you be willing to share a few tips
> with me on how to go about doing it??
>

Hi Paul,

If I am going to port my Windows (MF) Cobol GUI to Linux, this is
simply no conversion at all. Ubuntu Linux runs with "Wine" application
from within the Linux OS. So simply install the application using
Wine.... of course with MF, you need to install Application Server
module as well.

Tried running MF Cobol application from it and it works well. I do not
know OpenCOBOL though, but if you can manage to have a Cobol-GUI in
Windows using OpenCobol... might as well install it using wine and add
your application. No need of "OS-porting", it is all compatible in
Linux Wine.


Rene
```

```
Hi, all!

It's been a while since I posted on c.l.c.  I left the mainframe world

these skills and the times when I did use use them I didn't use them
```

```
(I was once asked Interview Question Number 17 (DB2 sheet) of 'What do you 
do to get a COBOL source-code file which contains SQL statements to run?'; 
my answer was 'Well, what *I* do is go into my library, grab the right 
compile skeleton, do a global replace on the member-name and SUB the 
result... but you're probably looking for the Textbook Answer of 
'Precompile, Compile, Link and Bind', right?'

I got the contract... but imagine what would have happened if the 
interviewer was not familiar with the steps of 'go into my library, grab 
the right compile skeleton, do a global replace on the member-name and SUB 
the result'.)

--end quoted text

DD
```

```
Started doing that a longer time ago, before there was such a thing as

and my response was along the lines of 'I'd ask to look into the lead 
programmer's library so that my version would look Just Like Everyone 
Else's... and if he refused I'd ask someone else... and if they all 
refused I'd check the system sample libraries... and if someone had RACF'd 
me out of all of those I'd grab my copy of Trombetta & Finklestein so that 
if what I did was wrong at least I'd be wrong according to the textbook...

... and if my copy of Trombetta & Finklestein wasn't around I'd quit the 
contract because I wouldn't work with thieves who'd steal my books... but 
you probably want to talk about boring things like what's important to 
include in the DELETE/DEFINE/REPRO steps, right?'

(That job I did *not* get... or rather, I did not take; turned out that 
while I was looking to be an independent they were looking for someone to 
be part of their stable, 'We'll keep paying you even if you're on the 
beach between contracts'... and the fellow blanched when I mentioned 
escrow accounts.)

you'll see I started with a triangle and then began to round the sides out 
so while it mostly works like a wheel it sometimes exhibits polygonal 
behavior... and that's good, except for the times when it happens at 2:am 
and they gotta call the New Kid to fix it... but everyone has to live 
through that, right, and besides... it's *my* wheel, not anyone else's!

DD
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Recommendation for refreshing and updating skills

- **From:** Michael Wojcik <mwojcik@newsguy.com>
- **Date:** 2009-02-20T13:52:15-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<gnn0fo020tn@news3.newsguy.com>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<1c2bd04b-76f8-421c-898e-79ff56c9c75b@40g2000prx.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<15555e7f-f5d3-4b4e-9622-f05b0b073bbb@r41g2000prr.googlegroups.com> <1c2bd04b-76f8-421c-898e-79ff56c9c75b@40g2000prx.googlegroups.com>`

```
scott97007@gmail.com wrote:
> 
> I wasn't able to find any inexpensive CICS emulators.  Do you think it
> would it be too difficult to write one?

"Too difficult" is a subjective evaluation. Would it be difficult?
Yes, quite.

>  At least one with enough
> functionality to practice basic transaction concepts?

A small team of very good developers, some of whom have written CICS
emulators in the past, can implement a minimal set of CICS
functionality in a few months.

Of course, anyone could read the CICS docs and create something that
acts as they think CICS should act, for some fraction of CICS
applications. Once the basic API infrastructure (macro processing,
CICS calling conventions, etc) is in place - not trivial, but doable -
you could stub out as many CICS macros and system calls as you like,
and have them return the "correct" value for inputs of your choosing.

Without a real CICS system to compare it to, though, how would you
know whether your mock-up was behaving like the real thing?

>  It wouldn't
> hurt too much if I went into an interview and mention that I practiced
> CICS on an emulator I wrote myself.  A preprocessor for "EXEC CICS"
> would not be to hard to write.

True, though it's more complicated than it looks at first blush. And
there's a lot that's not conceptually hard, but tiresome - predefined
constants and that sort of thing.

>  I think I could use a web server with
> PHP in place of SNA to handle the maps in and out.\

For simple pseudoconversational traffic, yes. For more complex
operations, the semantics of HTTP are wrong. That's why web-based
front-ending products for CICS (EnterpriseLink, OnWeb, etc) are
themselves pretty complex.

> I guess to partially answer my own question is that it depends on how
> much of CICS I want to emulate.

Definitely, though the preprocessor and the other elements of the API
interface (CICS constants, etc) aren't as amenable to partitioning -
you pretty much need most of that, or you don't have anything usable.

> What parts of CICS would be most useful to emulate?

Well, that's the rub. It depends on the parts of CICS that your
prospective employers 1) use and 2) would like you to know on the
first day. Do they use channels and containers? Do they use CICS Web
Services? Do they use EZASOKET? Do they use TS/TD? Do they use SPI
(the Systems Programming Interface)?

Those are all features that are outside the CICS "core", so to speak -
a lot of classic CICS apps would never use any of them - but I see
customers using them extensively in the CICS applications that they're
trying to maintain and modernize. Where there are CICS jobs, they
often seem to emphasize newer or more esoteric CICS features;
precisely because if you're going to maintain CICS apps, you might as
well bring them up to date.

That said, I don't want to discourage you from trying to write your
own emulator. It's an interesting project (interesting to me, anyway).
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Recommendation for refreshing and updating skills

- **From:** scott97007@gmail.com
- **Date:** 2009-02-20T14:51:39-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1d1e3f2a-ac83-4341-9bc7-357eac814ac8@w34g2000yqm.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<15555e7f-f5d3-4b4e-9622-f05b0b073bbb@r41g2000prr.googlegroups.com> <1c2bd04b-76f8-421c-898e-79ff56c9c75b@40g2000prx.googlegroups.com>`

```

To practice JCL, I’ll set up Hercules with MVS. I just have to figure

or MVS. For my purposes it won’t work for DB2 and CICS work.  To get
started, I'll use MicroFocus' free edition. zCOBOL will be coming out
in early March, and it may be closer to a true mainframe compiler, so
I may be using this more after it's out.

For DB2, I’ll use IBM’s free version. MicroFocus works with DB2. I’m
not sure about zCOBOL, but unless they add "EXEC SQL" support to z390,
I don’t believe it will. "EXEC SQL" is still on the to-do list for
z390, and until it’s in z390, I doubt it will go into zCOBOL.

For CICS, there is a CICS transaction server for z390. The instruction
set is limited, but it should have enough functionality to do basic
CICS style programming. The zCOBOL compiler will work with this psuedo-
CICS environment.  I don't know if MicroFocus will.

Just getting all of this set up an running on a PC should make me
stand out in an interview.

Don Higgins and the guys who support the z390 project deserve a gold
medal or something for all the great work they’ve done. Same goes for
the Hercules folks.  And you too Bill.

Shees! How many people really thought we’d be running mainframes on
our desktop PCs for free in the year 2009?
```

## Thread: z/OS Cobol source libraries — 8 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### z/OS Cobol source libraries

- **From:** "Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com>
- **Date:** 2009-02-18T17:40:22-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<499C4806.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com>`

```
Here's maybe a silly question, but...

For z/OS Cobol users, do you normally store your Cobol copybooks in the same
library (PDS/PDSE) as your Cobol source members, or in a different library?

What are the good and bad points of one over the other?

Frank
```

#### ↳ Re: z/OS Cobol source libraries

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2009-02-19T01:31:58+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<gnicqe$9lk$2@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<499C4806.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com>`

```
In article <499C4806.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com>,
Frank Swarbrick <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote:
>Here's maybe a silly question, but...
>
>For z/OS Cobol users, do you normally store your Cobol copybooks in the same
>library (PDS/PDSE) as your Cobol source members, or in a different library?

I follow the conventions encountered at the client's site.

>
>What are the good and bad points of one over the other?

The good point about doing what everyone else is doing is that it usually 
makes the person who has the most say over signing checks for the systems 
to smile.

Now I know you're 'just asking'... but here's a freebie: if copybooks are 
all kept in a single PDS to which programmers have only read access then 
the likelihood of someone mashing a good version with a bad one decreases.  
If a copybook needs changing then at least four eyes - the coder's and the 
person with update access to the PDS - might give the work a going-over.

(Books have been written and courses offered about the arcane art of 
Version Control... and they usually get forgotten because, as we all know, 
Things Are Different Here and this has to go into Prod now Now NOW!)

DD
```

#### ↳ Re: z/OS Cobol source libraries

- **From:** Arnold Trembley <arnold.trembley@worldnet.att.net>

```
Frank Swarbrick wrote:
> Here's maybe a silly question, but...
> 
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> Frank

At my shop copybooks are stored in a separate library, one where the 
last node of the dataset name is "MACLIB".  While I am comfortable with 
this approach, there is one disadvantage - it allows programmers to 
create a copybook with the same name as a COBOL source program, which I 
consider to be a bad practice.

My guess would be that having copybooks in a separate library is the 
more common practice in z/OS shops, but I could be wrong.
```

#### ↳ Re: z/OS Cobol source libraries

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2009-02-19T02:33:11-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<dP8nl.208765$9i5.206099@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<499C4806.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com>`

```
Frank,
  As I know that you are "setting up" a new z/OS environment, what you "should" 
do may differ from shops that have inherited (for decades) how they do things.

It has been a LONG time since I actually worked in a production z/OS (MVS-ish) 
environment. Therefore, I will happily yield to Arnold and Doc who have more 
current experience that I do.  However, when I did, it seemed that most (large?) 
shops had 3rd product source code control systems (originally, Panvalet and 
Librarian, then Endeavor, then others) - or at LEAST used SCLM.  With the 3rd 
party products, there were significant advantages in that you could (relatively 
easily) get back to earlier versions of source - when a "mistake" was 
introduced.

If you ever see COBOL source code with
  ++INCLUDE
or
 -INC

These were "equivalent" (sort-of) to COPY statements.  However, with later 
versions of those products you could "process" a member via a COPY statement and 
the product had vendor-supplied "access methods" to make their proprietary 
libraries look like "normal" PDS's.

All of this is to say, that (if what I remember is still current practice at 
many shops), your original assumption that source code was in PDS's is where the 
"error" is.  When you use the source control systems, "naming" and where you 
store things becomes a different question.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: z/OS Cobol source libraries

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2009-02-19T14:20:50+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<gnjps2$7i0$1@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<499C4806.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com> <dP8nl.208765$9i5.206099@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
In article <dP8nl.208765$9i5.206099@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com>,
William M. Klein <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com> wrote:

[snip]

>It has been a LONG time since I actually worked in a production z/OS (MVS-ish) 
>environment.

Such modesty ill-becomes you, Mr Klein... really, it's just like riding a 
bicycle... you get the fire going, heat up the water in the boiler, adjust 
the valves so the driveshaft gets sufficient power to start moving, make 
sure the fireman keeps the box filled...

... a steam-powered bicycle, that is.

>Therefore, I will happily yield to Arnold and Doc who have more 
>current experience that I do.  However, when I did, it seemed that most
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>introduced.

Anyone remember the 1980s buzz-phrase of 'we get it right the first time, 
we can't afford to make mistakes'?  The primary advantage of source-code 
configuration systems - be they system-based or a crotechty old coot who 
'signs out' code to you is that they encourage efficient co-ordination of 
maintenance and decrease the probability that two programmers, unbeknownst 
to each other, are assigned to work on the same module.

The primary disadvantage is, of course, they Cost Money and folks still 
manage to find work-arounds that can cause grave difficulties.  My current 
client's site uses CA-LIBRARIAN and two Librarian source libraries, 
HIGHNODE.DEVMAINT.SOURCE and HIGHNODE.PRODUCTN.SOURCE, with only Ops 
having write access to the latter.  Both libraries contain source and 
copybooks... but when in Rome one toddles toga-clad.

When I am told a module needs maintaining/enhancing the first thing I do 
is make copies of both the DEVMAINT and PRODUCTN versions to my own PDS 
(USERID.LIB.COBOL) and run a SuperC compare against them; if all is well 
and good the modules are identical.  I then do what needs to be done, 
compile with my own JCL to my own USERID.TEST.LOADLIB and test... and 
curse... and re-mod, compile, test, curse, etc... until I am satisfied 
with the results.

I then copy what I believe to be my properly-changed code into the 
DEVMAINT library, compile it there using standardised JCL, test again and 
then notify Whoever Needs To Be Told that I'm ready to have someone else 
break my code.  Sometimes they need to do minimal testing - 'the group 
that uses the code was re-assigned and the Department Name needs to be 
changed, leave everything else as is' - and other times it can get a bit 
scary, along the lines of 'Sixteen counties in four states need to have 
taxes re-calculated BUT ONLY IF the employee has an even number of 
children with a total number of teeth which, when divided by three, leaves 
behind no remainder'... at which point someone will ask me for the names 
of the files I cobbled together to do my own testing and grab copies of 
them... but never mind that.

Once the DEVMAINT testing is done the module is copied to the PRODUCTN 
library and recompiled into .PRODUCTN.LOAD ... and life runs on.

DD
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: z/OS Cobol source libraries

- **From:** Arnold Trembley <arnold.trembley@worldnet.att.net>
- **Date:** 2009-02-20T07:37:04+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<A4tnl.388365$Mh5.24648@bgtnsc04-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<dP8nl.208765$9i5.206099@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<499C4806.6F0F.0085.0@efirstbank.com> <dP8nl.208765$9i5.206099@en-nntp-07.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
William M. Klein wrote:
> Frank,
>   As I know that you are "setting up" a new z/OS environment, what you "should" 
…[25 more quoted lines elided]…
> 

The z/OS shop where I work uses Endevor to manage source code and 
executable objects.  Endevor can be configured in many ways, but we have 
six stages from Test to Prod.  Production COBOL source code is stored in 
  PDS libraries that are exclusively managed by Endevor.  When we 
"retrieve" a COBOL program (with or without "sign-out") we store it in a 
PDS where we can play with it.  The PDS would be named something like 
"HIGHNODE.TEST.PDSLIB" so any programmer could use it or "USERID.COBOL" 
so only I can read it.

We used to have Panvalet, but replaced it with Endevor over 10 years 
ago.  Our Endevor is configured to manage source files as "elements" by 
"element type", which we have named as follows:

COB	COBOL source code
ASM	Assembly language
EZT	Easytrieve
CPY	Copybooks (for COB, ASM, or EZT)
JCL	Job Control Language
PRC	JCL Procedures called by JCL
CRD	Control Card files called by JCL and PRC
DOC	Operational documentation for JCL jobs
LNK	Link Edit control statements for specific builds
PKG	DB2 Package control statements

Our Endevor is configured so that ADDing a program to the first Test 
stage requires a compile, and the generated executable is moved to the 
next higher stage whenever the source code is promoted.  Endevor could 
be configured to automatically recompile every time the source is 
promoted to a higher stage, but our management decided that we only 
wanted to promote tested load modules.  Recompiling at every stage might 
make it a little easier to manage copybook changes in sync with program 
changes.

The generated result of an Endevor-controlled COBOL compile is an 
executable load module, in stage 6 that would be one of two PDS 
libaries, either HIGHNODE.PROD.LOADLIB or HIGHNODE.CICS.PROD.LOADLIB. 
But for intermediate stages we have different names such as TEST or CERT 
or PROD in the PDS library name.  But copybooks are generated to 
HIGHNODE.TEST.MACLIB or HIGHNODE.PROD.MACLIB as needed, so they can be 
available for compiles.  Similarly, control card modules are generated 
eventually to HIGHNODE.PROD.CARDLIB, procs to HIGHNODE.PROD.PROCLIB, JCL 
to HIGHNODE.PROD.JCLLIB, and operational documentation to 
HIGHNODE.PROD.DOCLIB.

A DOC file has the same name as a JCL source file, and contains 
scheduling and restart instructions for the operators.

You must specify a "Processor" name when compiling a COBOL program into 
Endevor, because the processor script must be different for batch or 
CICS, for different COBOL compilers, for DB2 or non-DB2, and for 
Debugger support or no debugger support.  And CICS programs must be 
generated into HIGHNODE.CICS.PROD.LOADLIB while batch COBOL programs are 
generated into HIGHNODE.PROD.LOADLIB.

All this might or might not be helpful to Frank Swarbrick.  A friend of 
mine who worked for a retail chain converted their small IBM mainframe 
from DOS/VSE to z/OS and found the use of JCL versus PROCs confusing. 
It was very different from the way they managed DOS/VSE JCL.  They also 
had very few standard naming conventions for source files or data files, 
which made it harder to manage their security rules.

Endevor also supports recovery of earlier versions of source code, and 
even automatic backout of executable programs.  SCLM is from IBM, and I 
believe it is included with TSO/ISPF on z/OS, but I don't know if it 
manages executables in addition to source code.

Endevor is a big, complicated tool and I haven't even addressed the 
problem of naming conventions for programs, JCL, procs, and copybooks, 
or other issues like nested procs in production JCL, or Security/audit 
control procedures for installing objects into production.  Object 
naming conventions can have a large effect on your RACF/ACF2/TOP Secret 
security administration rules.  You can guess that I work in a fairly 
big shop that has to comply with GLBA, SOX, and PCI-DSS.  While I am 
used to the way we do things there is absolutely no guarantee there 
isn't a better way to organize it, or better naming standards to use.

If all I had to do was code and test COBOL programs my job would be much 
easier.

With kindest regards,
```

## Thread: Creating COBOL real-time software on Windows... — 30 msgs

### Creating COBOL real-time software on Windows...

- **From:** Kellie Fitton <KELLIEFITTON@YAHOO.COM>
- **Date:** 2009-02-19T12:46:04-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<2d88f288-9812-4ffb-b726-932bff86d3f9@p20g2000yqi.googlegroups.com>`

```
Hi,

Since Windows OS is not a real-time operating system but
rather a multitasking environment,   Is there a way to have
mighty COBOL declares my tables in the working-storage
section as real-time constructs ?

My COBOL software has a GUI interface and is designed for
multi-users environment, and it requires an instant response
and interaction between users and muliple sub-programs.

I think if my COBOL application gets a small time slice (20 ms),
then it can Emulate a real-time application and should handle
the keyboard/mouse instantly enough to process the work load.

Thank you...
```

#### ↳ Re: Creating COBOL real-time software on Windows...

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <mmattias@talsystems.com>

```
"Kellie Fitton" <KELLIEFITTON@YAHOO.COM> wrote in message 
news:2d88f288-9812-4ffb-b726-932bff86d3f9@p20g2000yqi.googlegroups.com...
> Hi,
>
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
> the keyboard/mouse instantly enough to process the work load.

Let's play a game called "Truth *AND* Consequences, shall we?

TRUTH: Yes, you can make your program operate under Windows on a real-time 
priority basis. No I am not going to tell you how, because if you take my 
advice in the last paragraph you will learn how to do that.

CONSEQUENCES: If you worked for me and did so, you would no longer work for 
me.

Let Windows handle the time-slicing, it really does do a hell of a good job 
unless you program like a schmuck, in which case you would no longer work 
for me.

If your program requires 'instant' response (requiring real time prioirty), 
then you have designed like a schmuck and you no longer work as a designer 
for me, although you may continue to work as a programmer, unless we''ve 
already made that a non-starter for one of the above reasons.  Oops, wait a 
minute.... your comments re "multi-users environment" leads me to believe 
you do not understand the Windows' environment very well, in which case we 
have to rule out that designer position anyway.

Well, Ok, here's some free advice, which is worth a hell of lot more than 
you are paying for it: you need to study up on multi-threaded applications 
under Windows, because that's IMO the best way to handle things when you 
need a responsive GUI with a time-consuming "work load" associated with 
various user actions.
```

```
Kellie Fitton wrote:
> On Feb 19, 1:15 pm, "Michael Mattias" <mmatt...@talsystems.com> wrote:
>> "Kellie Fitton" <KELLIEFIT...@YAHOO.COM> wrote in message
…[67 more quoted lines elided]…
> Kellie.

OK, to answer the question:

1. There is no way I am aware of to dynamically declare tabes in COBOL. 
(Various systms allow dynamic allocation of memory by calling low level 
functions, but even having acquired the memory, you strill can't dynamicaly 
declare the tables...)
2. You CAN get the same effect by coding your tables into called modules 
which have no action in the procedure division. Then you can reference your 
table at run time with a CALL... USING.

This will allow you to have REFERENCE tables immediately available, but you 
cannot grow them. Still, you might be able to adapt this idea to what you DO 
need...).

HTH

Pete.
```

```
"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message 
news:7066adFn368hU1@mid.individual.net...
> Kellie Fitton wrote:
>>>> Since Windows OS is not a real-time operating system but
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> dynamicaly declare the tables...)

You can do it by using
01  MY-TABLE     USAGE POINTER

(or equivalent)  .. and allocating from the far heap (about 32 different 
ways to do that)

HOWEVER.... it offers no advantages.

All memory under Win/32 is virtual. Windows controls what swaps in and what 
swaps out.

Besides, if you think you need 2GB of table data in RAM, you designed like a 
schmuck.

> 2. You CAN get the same effect by coding your tables into called modules 
> which have no action in the procedure division. Then you can reference 
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> you DO need...).

That doesn't do any good Pete... called modules are part of the single 
process' address space and are subject to the same features, benefits and 
restrictions as any other user memory.

All that said, take a look at creating a memory-mapped file object for your 
tables. That may be useful.
```

```
A very good post, Michael. Firm but fair... :-)

Kellie, I suspect that most of what you have is using the Windows API? (I 
also think it is very impressive that you have reached the stage you have 
from being a novice a couple of years ago.)

When you are dealing at a low level (as you are when you use the Windows API 
directly) although you get access to some very useful functionality, it is 
easy to lose sight of the "bigger picture"... like not seeing the wood for 
the trees... Michael is absolutely right that the "administrative functions" 
concerning tasks are best left to the OS. (And despite all the Windows 
hatred out there, it really is very good at this.) Only under really 
exceptional circumstances (I'm thinking real time control flows in an oil 
refinery, critical device feedback loops on a manufacturing line... that 
sort of thing...) might you consider messing with this and even then you 
need to have a very good understanding of exactly what it is you are messing 
with.

If I were you, I'd take Michael's advice and read about threading and 
priority. Then, if you want to experiment, well, Hey, it's your system, and 
presumably you havea test incarnation of it...

Good luck and have fun :-)

Pete.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Creating COBOL real-time software on Windows...

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <mmattias@talsystems.com>
- **Date:** 2009-02-20T09:15:54-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<wMznl.2281$Lr6.1658@flpi143.ffdc.sbc.com>`
- **References:** `<2d88f288-9812-4ffb-b726-932bff86d3f9@p20g2000yqi.googlegroups.com> <e_jnl.5629$%54.2852@nlpi070.nbdc.sbc.com> <706504Fn1jmoU1@mid.individual.net> <bdc635ae-7b43-4ec8-af0a-9fcfa5d436b4@r29g2000vbp.googlegroups.com>`

```
"Kellie Fitton" <KELLIEFITTON@YAHOO.COM> wrote in message 
news:bdc635ae-7b43-4ec8-af0a-9fcfa5d436b4@r29g2000vbp.googlegroups.com...

> I used the Win32 APIs CreateThread(), SetThreadPriority(), and
>SetPriorityClass() to create threads and set the
>priority/class value.

>This is my own test version of it and I am trying
>to find out if COBOL has a way of declaring all my
>arrays or tables as real-time tables, so that it
>matches the priority class for a specified process.

Under Windows, there is no such thing as "real time memory."  There is only 
virtual memory (RAM) and secondary memory ( disk or other media).

Memory does not have a priority class. I don't know what you think 
SetThreadPriority() and SetPriorityClass() do, but if you think they have 
anything to do with memory, you should not be using these functions.  Play 
with matches, you can get burned.

Just write your program using good COBOL programming techiniques and the 
perfromance will take care of itself, if you let Windows handle it.

Some wag (that would be me) once published an article on the subject of 
optimization.  In that piece I posited the two most important things 
would-be 'optimizers' should do:

1. Remember all optimization is application-specific... there is no silver 
bullet.
2. First you make it work; only then do you make it work better.
```

#### ↳ Re: Creating COBOL real-time software on Windows...

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2009-02-19T15:11:54-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<60e762d0-b4e7-4e84-adc2-4292f60ccde7@q30g2000prq.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<2d88f288-9812-4ffb-b726-932bff86d3f9@p20g2000yqi.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Feb 20, 9:46 am, Kellie Fitton <KELLIEFIT...@YAHOO.COM> wrote:
> Hi,
>
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> section as real-time constructs ?

Are you referring to 'tables' as arrays, eg OCCURS nn, or as SQL
database tables, or perhaps even indexed file ?

What do you mean when you use the term 'real-time constructs' ?

Is it that you want a database to be accessible as a set of arrays in
the working-storage of your program and these to be updated from other
computers as they amend or enter data ????


> My COBOL software has a GUI interface and is designed for
> multi-users environment, and it requires an instant response
> and interaction between users and muliple sub-programs.

What do you mean by 'instant', and more importantly, what is it that
is not currently 'instant'.


> I think if my COBOL application gets a small time slice (20 ms),
> then it can Emulate a real-time application and should handle
> the keyboard/mouse instantly enough to process the work load.

Why do you think that 'real-time' is necessary, or even useful ?

What is the 'workload' and why do you think that 20ms is sufficient ?
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Creating COBOL real-time software on Windows...

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <mmattias@talsystems.com>
- **Date:** 2009-02-20T09:07:40-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<wMznl.2280$Lr6.320@flpi143.ffdc.sbc.com>`
- **References:** `<2d88f288-9812-4ffb-b726-932bff86d3f9@p20g2000yqi.googlegroups.com> <60e762d0-b4e7-4e84-adc2-4292f60ccde7@q30g2000prq.googlegroups.com> <4b6fc16a-cf55-4e60-863c-64d460367120@l39g2000yqn.googlegroups.com> <qGqnl.99068$pp1.97396@en-nntp-06.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
"William M. Klein" <wmklein@nospam.ix.netcom.com> wrote in message 
news:qGqnl.99068$pp1.97396@en-nntp-06.dc1.easynews.com...
> My best bet is that this is irrelevant, but as someone who has never coded 
> multi-threaded COBOL applications,
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> raise this as a possibility.

Threads are owned by processes, meaning all the process' data are available 
for use within the context of any thread of execution of that process. 
Windows does offer some special facilitues, specifically Thread Local 
Storage, to assist in managing data which much be unique to each thread of 
execution.

The memory-mapped file object I mentioned earlier is what can be used to 
share primary (RAM) memory across processes. However, that cannot share data 
across computers.

The whole idea of "multiple users" under Windows means multiple PROCESSES on 
a single computer

If you want to talk about many computers requiring access to the same data, 
then you can do what you do on any operating system... you can share disk 
files, or create some kind of client-server system in whcih the server 
handles all the storage and retrival.

How these features are implemented by various COBOL compilers is unknown to 
me... after all, I have not used any COBOL since 2001.  But I work with 
these Windows processes/threads things essentially every day.
```

```
On Feb 20, 4:43 pm, Kellie Fitton <KELLIEFIT...@YAHOO.COM> wrote:

It seems that you want several machines, each running your program, to
load the indexed files into arrays into their working-storage and this
to be updated automatically by any one machine changing the data.

Presumably you want this to happen 'immediately' and without any
overhead or network traffic.

Given that we now know what you meant by 'real-time contructs' we can
now say that the answer is 'No'. You cannot simply put a keyword on an
array in Cobol which means 'do stuff that is impossible'.

In fact I don't think that there is _any_ mechanism in any language or
operating system will do what you seem to want.


> 4). Immediate response to events and processing of data
> and computations quickly to meet a deadline.

What is the 'deadline' and why ? Don't just say 'instant' or
'immediate' because these imply zero microseconds, give a number.

How is this to be measured ?

> 5). Concurrent access and the application has the needs
> to keep a number of connected systems up-to-date with
> changing situations.

Then you probably don't want a Windows program, you probably want a
server based system where, for example, a single application (which
may have multiple instatnces) updates the data from transactions sent
in from the remote computers and then it 'pushes' the changes out to
the client machines which are just displaying the information.

Perhaps you are trying to write something like a trading-floor system.


> 6). The workload is look-up reference tables, computations,
> managing/updating indexed files, printing hard copies of
> documents/large reports, transfer/download of large files.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Creating COBOL real-time software on Windows...

- **From:** "HeyBub" <heybub@NOSPAMgmail.com>
- **Date:** 2009-02-20T07:41:29-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<2sqdna41Sr-QLgPUnZ2dnUVZ_v3inZ2d@earthlink.com>`
- **References:** `<2d88f288-9812-4ffb-b726-932bff86d3f9@p20g2000yqi.googlegroups.com> <60e762d0-b4e7-4e84-adc2-4292f60ccde7@q30g2000prq.googlegroups.com> <4b6fc16a-cf55-4e60-863c-64d460367120@l39g2000yqn.googlegroups.com>`

```
Kellie Fitton wrote:
> On Feb 19, 3:11 pm, Richard <rip...@Azonic.co.nz> wrote:
>> On Feb 20, 9:46 am, Kellie Fitton <KELLIEFIT...@YAHOO.COM> wrote:
…[41 more quoted lines elided]…
>

The OS is doing a lot down in the weeds that is invisible to the application 
program.

For very large tables, it is often faster just to fetch the damn record than 
to find it in the table.

This is because the operating system often has the required record cached in 
its buffers and doesn't actually have to read the file.

You can test this:
1. Get a record.
2. Start a timer
3. Get the same record 100,000 times
4. Stop the timer
5. Compute the elapsed time.

I'll wager the elapsed time is insignificant.

Of course you can simulate this in a table look-up also:

IF (requested record) = (last record requested)
   process record
ELSE
   do table-lookup.

The technique chosen often depends on the nature of the data. In one 
hospital billing program I worked on, it was obvious EVERYBODY had 
"Semi-private room" and "Telephone access" and a few other things every day! 
These were semi-hard-coded in the program and, by so doing, decreased the 
processing time dramatically.

--------
Aside:
Dimwits insisted on printing zero-balance statements. Since most charges 
were covered by insurance, 95% of the statements printed each week were zero 
(we're talking several tens of thousands of statements).

Sure enough, I had to visit the emergency room as a patient and paid my $30 
fee in cash. This resulted, in the fullness of time, in my receiving the 
aforementioned zero-balance statement.

Carefully noting the "Pay this amount - $0.00" line, I dutifully put a check 
for "Zero dollars and 00/100 dollars" in the reply envelope and sent it 
along. This activity caused much confusion in the ensuing months as I 
continually inquired of the billing office why my cancelled check had not 
been processed.
```

```
This can be a flaw rather than a feature. Where a file is on a server
and is shared and updated by various programs running on different
machines you do _not_ want it cached locally.

The problem that Kellie has, apparently, is that he wants to

the file that is on some central server so that he can display a
screenfull of information, but he doesn't want to have to read the

> been processed.

A statement is a 'statement of account', it is a listing of the
transactions for the account. It may (or need not) also contain a
request for payment of the outstanding amount. It is irrelevant that
the outstanding debt is zero, the transactions are still required to
be listed and communicated.

In one of my systems the statement program prints the final line as
"Please pay this amount $nnn.nn' or 'Thank you for your prompt
payment' or 'Your account is overdue, please pay $nnn.nn by dd/mm/yy'.

But then most people understand that 'please pay nothing' means
'payment is not required'.
```

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <mmattias@talsystems.com>

```
>The problem that Kellie has, apparently, is that he wants to
>continuously and immediately know the current state of all the data in
>the file that is on some central server so that he can display a
>screenfull of information, but he doesn't want to have to read the
>whole file in every display cycle.

>He wants the client machines kept up to date magically, whereas your
>caching would keep refreshing with old data.

FWIW, under Windows you can set up a ChangeNotification object and receive a 
notification in your program whenever a 'file of intrerest' is updated.

The 'notification' is actually done at the FOLDER level, you'll have to 
check the timestamp of the target file against your last timestamp to know 
if the 'file of interest" in the "watched folder for which a change 
notification was received"  is the file in that folder which has changed.
```
